## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy HTTP Filter Chain Registration and Execution

## Your Task

Trace how HTTP filter chains are registered and executed in the Envoy proxy. Find C++ and protobuf files across envoyproxy/envoy and envoyproxy/data-plane-api that implement: the FilterChainFactory interface (in envoy/http/), the FilterChainHelper that constructs chains from config, the FilterManager that executes filter chains at runtime, and the HttpConnectionManager proto that defines the filter_chain configuration schema.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

Http::FilterChainFactory - provides createFilterChain() method\\n2. Http::ConnectionManagerConfig - provides general connection management configuration\\n\\nDuring initialization (config.cc:709-715), a FilterChainHelper template class is instantiated with the proto configuration. Calls manager.applyFilterFactoryCb() for each enabled filter, passing the FilterFactoryCb\\n\\n## Filter Chain Management at Runtime\\n\\nThe FilterChainManager interface (envoy/http/filter_factory.h:70-81) provides the `applyFilterFactoryCb()` method that receives filter factory callbacks. The FilterManager class (source/common/http/filter_manager.h:638-700) implements FilterChainManager and:\\n1. Receives FilterFactoryCb via applyFilterFactoryCb()\\n2. Invokes the callback with FilterChainFactoryCallbacks to add decoded/encoder filters\\n3. Maintains separate lists of decoder and encoder filters\\n\\nThe DownstreamFilterManager (source/common/http/filter_manager.h:1094-1150) is a specialized FilterManager for downstream (client-facing) connections that adds local reply handling capabilities.\\n\\n## Execution Flow\\n\\nAt runtime, FilterManager::createFilterChain() (filter_manager.cc:1550-1560) is called when headers are received. This:\\n1. Ensures createFilterChain is only called once\\n2. Triggers filter chain instantiation through the FilterChainFactory\\n3. Builds the active filter chain by calling each FilterFactoryCb\\n4. Filters are added via addStreamDecoderFilter() or addStreamEncoderFilter() (filter_manager.h:672-693)\\n\\nExecution proceeds through the filter chain via iteration methods (maybeContinueDecoding, maybeContinueEncoding) that pass request headers, body data, and trailers through filters in sequence, respecting filter return codes (Continue, StopIteration, etc.).\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n1. **Two-Phase Construction**: Configuration parsing (FilterChainHelper) is separate from runtime chain building (FilterManager)\\n2. **Factory Pattern**: FilterFactoryCb callbacks enable lazy, configurable filter instantiation\\n3. **Callback-Based Chaining**: Filters communicate through FilterChainManager's applyFilterFactoryCb interface\\n4. **Separation of Concerns**: Network-level FilterChain management is distinct from HTTP-level FilterChain execution\"\n}\n",
